        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932"><meta property="og:title" content="Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/acs.nanolett.6b02932.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Simultaneous integration of high-energy output with high-power delivery is a major challenge for electrochemical energy storage systems, limiting dual fine attributes on a device. We introduce a quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor (NIC) based on a battery type urchin-like Na2Ti3O7 anode and a capacitor type peanut shell derived carbon cathode, using a sodium ion conducting gel polymer as electrolyte, achieving high-energy-high-power characteristics in solid state. Energy densities can reach 111.2 Wh kg–1 at power density of 800 W kg–1, and 33.2 Wh kg–1 at power density of 11200 W kg–1, which are among the best reported state-of-the-art NICs. The designed device also exhibits long-term cycling stability over 3000 cycles with capacity retention ∼86%. Furthermore, we demonstrate the assembly of a highly flexible quasi-solid-state NIC and it shows no obvious capacity loss under different bending conditions."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/acs.nanolett.6b02932.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '78742923-dfc6-4610-801a-6ddd9c2dc837'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'nano_letters';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/nano_letters/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/nano_letters/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

title="Download Hi-Res Image" target="_blank" class="figure-viewer_hi-res-link"><i class="icon-file-image-o"></i><span>Download Hi-Res Image</span></a><span class="fv-separator"></span><a href="#" title="Download to MS-PowerPoint" class="figure-viewer_ms-p-link"><i class="icon-file-powerpoint-o"></i><span>Download to MS-PowerPoint</span></a><span class="cit-this-container"><a href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite This:</strong></span></a><span class="article_header-cite-this figure-viewer-cite-this"><span class="cit-fg-title"><i>Nano Lett.</i></span><span class="cit-fg-year"> 2016</span><span class="cit-fg-volume">, 16</span><span class="cit-fg-issue">, 9</span><span class="cit-fg-pageRange">, 5938-5943</span></span></span></div></div></div></div></div><input type="hidden" name="nalefd" id="copyRights" value="/pb-assets/json/journal-info-1738870756703.json"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone5" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone5"><!-- Article Refresh Event Tracking -->
<script nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "nalefd";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Energy–High-Power Density in a Flexible Quasi-Solid-State Sodium Ion Capacitor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D5938%26pageCount%3D6%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHongsen%2BLi%252C%2BLele%2BPeng%252C%2BYue%2BZhu%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D9%26contentID%3Dacs.nanolett.6b02932%26title%3DAchieving%2BHigh-Energy%25E2%2580%2593High-Power%2BDensity%2Bin%2Ba%2BFlexible%2BQuasi-Solid-State%2BSodium%2BIon%2BCapacitor%26numPages%3D6%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1530-6984%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dnalefd%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D5943%26publicationDate%3DSeptember%2B2016" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/medium/nl-2016-02932h_0005.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Simultaneous integration of high-energy output with high-power delivery is a major challenge for electrochemical energy storage systems, limiting dual fine attributes on a device. We introduce a quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor (NIC) based on a battery type urchin-like Na<sub>2</sub>Ti<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub> anode and a capacitor type peanut shell derived carbon cathode, using a sodium ion conducting gel polymer as electrolyte, achieving high-energy-high-power characteristics in solid state. Energy densities can reach 111.2 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at power density of 800 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, and 33.2 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at power density of 11200 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, which are among the best reported state-of-the-art NICs. The designed device also exhibits long-term cycling stability over 3000 cycles with capacity retention ∼86%. Furthermore, we demonstrate the assembly of a highly flexible quasi-solid-state NIC and it shows no obvious capacity loss under different bending conditions.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D5938%26pageCount%3D6%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHongsen%2BLi%252C%2BLele%2BPeng%252C%2BYue%2BZhu%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D9%26contentID%3Dacs.nanolett.6b02932%26title%3DAchieving%2BHigh-Energy%25E2%2580%2593High-Power%2BDensity%2Bin%2Ba%2BFlexible%2BQuasi-Solid-State%2BSodium%2BIon%2BCapacitor%26numPages%3D6%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1530-6984%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dnalefd%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D5943%26publicationDate%3DSeptember%2B2016" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2016 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290916&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Capacitors" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Capacitors" class="article__tags__link">Capacitors</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292120&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrolytes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrolytes" class="article__tags__link">Electrolytes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290667&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Ions" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Ions" class="article__tags__link">Ions</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291251&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Sodium" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Sodium" class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium+Ion+Capacitor&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Sodium%20ion%20capacitor">Sodium ion capacitor</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Solid-state&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_solid-state">solid-state</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Conducting+Gel+Polymer&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_conducting%20gel%20polymer">conducting gel polymer</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High-energy+Density&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high-energy%20density">high-energy density</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High-power+Density&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high-power%20density">high-power density</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Energy+Storage&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_energy%20storage">energy storage</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><p class="first">Because of the limited natural resources and serious warming threats in the global scale, it is desperately required for human beings to cope with the environmental and energy problems. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1, 2)</a> Accordingly, in the near future it will be necessary to build a carbon-reducing society supported by the renewable energy such as wind, wave, and solar. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3 ref4'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 3 and 4">(3, 4)</a> The utilization of these intermittent energy resources highlights the need for high-performance cost-effective electrochemical storage devices that are able to store and deliver energy efficiently. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5" aria-label="reference 5">(5)</a> Supercapacitors, which have matured significantly over the past decade, could be a viable solution. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7" aria-label="reference 6 and 7">(6, 7)</a> They store charges through accumulation of ions at the high-surface area carbon surface (nonfaradaic surface reactions), providing the abilities that can be charged and discharged rapidly with long-term lifetime. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8" aria-label="reference 8">(8)</a> In view of that, when combined with the renewable energy resources supercapacitors can potentially demonstrate their effectiveness and merits. Aside from the above advantages, the low-energy density characteristics seriously restrict their further development. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> Alternatively, rechargeable ion batteries show competitive superiority in energy density through faradaic ion insertion reactions but the power density and cycle life of the batteries are far from satisfactory. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 10 and 11">(10, 11)</a> As a result, it is urgent to develop the future energy storage systems, combining the complementary features of high-power supercapacitor and high-energy rechargeable ion batteries, for many applications from portable electronics to public transportation in which high-energy–high-power delivery and uptake and long-term cycle life are required. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a></p><p>Recently, lithium ion capacitors have been explored to achieve the desired performance and become the focus of the researchers to realize different storage mechanisms at both electrodes in a device, wherein the supercapacitor type cathode endures fast charge–discharge processes, and the rechargeable ion battery type anode stores large capacitance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13 ref14 ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 13 to 15">(13-15)</a> For example, the lithium ion capacitor based on TiC//pyridine derived carbon (in 1 mol L<sup>–1</sup> LiPF<sub>6</sub> solution/ethylene carbonate electrolyte) delivered an energy density of 101.5 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> (achieved at 450 W kg<sup>–1</sup>) and an outstanding cycle stability (∼82% retention after 5000 cycles) within the voltage range of 0.0–4.5 V. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> At the same time, the fact that easily accessible global lithium reserves largely exist in a politically sensitive or a remote area drives the research toward energy storage systems beyond lithium ions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17 ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 17 to 19">(17-19)</a> Accordingly, replacing lithium with sodium to construct the sodium ion capacitors offers the opportunity to build the device integrated with the features of potentially lower cost and high performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> In the past three years, the sodium ion capacitor technology has gained great advances and the performance can also be comparable to lithium ion capacitors. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref21 ref22 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 5 and 21 to 23">(5, 21-23)</a> Lim et al. reported a type of sodium ion capacitor based on Nb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>@C/rGO-50 anode and activated carbon (MSP20) cathode in 1 mol L<sup>–1</sup> NaPF<sub>6</sub> solution/ethylene carbonate/dimethyl carbonate electrolyte. The device delivered a maximum energy density of approximately 76 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> with the power density of approximately 80 W kg<sup>–1</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> However, most of the hybrid devices explored thus far used the liquid electrolytes, which leads to a concern about potential safety. For these hybrid devices, their electrolytes are almost universally based on combinations of liner and cyclic alkyl carbonates. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> The high volatility and flammability of these organic electrolytes pose a serious safety issue for their use in the consumer (especially for flexible and wearable applications) and transportation markets. Hence, an efficient solution to avoid these crucial risks is realizing solid-state storage devices using solid-state electrolytes or quasi-solid-state electrolytes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a></p><p>Herein, we design a quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor based on an urchin-like Na<sub>2</sub>Ti<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub> (NTO) battery-type anode and peanut shell derived carbon (PSC) supercapacitor-type cathode. A kind of sodium ion conducting gel polymer using the P(VDF-HFP) membrane as the matrix was used as the electrolyte. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> The designed hybrid device integrated the advantages of both the sodium ion batteries and the supercapacitors, pushing the energy density, power density, and safety to a high level. We further assembled a flexible quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor, which has not been reported previously on the hybrid device. To produce the urchin-like NTO, a facile hydrothermal method combined with heat treatment was employed (see Experimental Section for more details, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). Shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a is scanning electron microscopy (SEM) image of the prepared NTO products, revealing an urchin-like morphology. The scanning transmission electron microscopy (STEM) image in Figure S1 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>) further reveals that the diameter of NTO nanofibers on the surface of NTO microspheres is in the range of 10–20 nm. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b presents an X-ray diffraction (XRD) pattern of the resultant urchin-like NTO indexed to PDF file 59-0666, implying that the hydrothermal products are pure phase of NTO. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> Furthermore, <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b insert schematically shows the crystal structure of NTO along the <i>a</i>-axis. The basic unit is a block of six TiO<sub>6</sub> octahedrons, which extend out of the plane as a zigzag ribbon of octahedrons limited to three in width. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref30" aria-label="reference 29 and 30">(29, 30)</a> A two-dimensional sheet of the composition (Ti<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub>)<sup>2–</sup> centered on the (100) plane is formed by the corner-shared identical blocks. Shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c is the SEM of the PSC, resembling a macroscopically open sponge morphology. The corresponding XRD pattern of the PSC shows two inconspicuous broad diffraction peaks that are indexed as (002) and (100), indicative of its much lower ordering. The nitrogen adsorption–desorption characterization is also measured and the results are shown in Figure S2 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). Specifically, the BET surface area is 1900.5 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> and total pore volume is 0.86 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> with an average pore diameter of 1.94 nm, indicative of the considerable porosity and high surface areas of the PSC.</p><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/medium/nl-2016-02932h_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a,b) SEM image and XRD pattern of urchin-like NTO and inset shows the crystallographic arrangements of NTO. (c,d) SEM and XRD pattern of PSC cathode material. The scale bars in (a,c) are 500 nm.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The electrochemical properties of the NTO anode and PSC cathode are evaluated by a constant charge–discharge test in half cells using the sodium ion conducting gel polymer as the electrolyte. Shown in Figure S3 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>) are the SEM images of the P(VDF-HFP) membrane, which is the matrix of the quasi-solid-state electrolyte before gelling. There are abundant pores on the surface of the membrane with the diameter of 1–2 μm that is beneficial to absorb and retain the organic electrolyte. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a shows the representative charge–discharge profiles of the NTO anode at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> between 0.01 and 2.5 V. A reversible capacity of 227 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> can be achieved, and it shows smooth curves, little polarization, and a low average operating voltage of ∼0.35 V. The first charge–discharge curves of the NTO anode are shown in Figure S4a (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). Further rate tests reveal that the urchin-like NTO enables a high rate capability, providing high-cycling stability with rapid changes of the current densities. It demonstrates a stable capacity of 210 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at the current density of 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup> and 200, 192, 188, 184, and 175 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at current density of 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, 1, and 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. It is believed that the present urchin-like NTO is a promising battery-type electrode in the hybrid ion capacitors that necessitate a high-power anode with high rate capability to balance the kinetics gap between the slow faradaic anode and the fast physical capacitor type cathode in order to optimize the energy and power densities. Shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c is the long-term cycling performance of the NTO at a current density of 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The capacity retention is 95.1% after 1000 cycles, corresponding to a very low-capacity fading rate. This cycling stability of these urchin-like NTO is superior to that of other reported NTO-based anode materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31 ref32 ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32 ref33" aria-label="reference 31 to 33">(31-33)</a> In addition, the cyclic voltammetry (CV) of the NTO is also tested and shown in Figure S5a (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). The typical charge–discharge curves of the PSC as the cathode are displayed in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d. It shows a large discharge capacity of 153 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with good reversibility. The rate capability of the PSC is also tested as shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>e. It is clear that the electrode displays stable capacities at each tested current density. The charge–discharge curves of PSC at different current densities are shown in Figure S6b (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>f demonstrates the cycling stability and the corresponding Coulombic efficiency of PSC. The electrode’s capacitance remains stable over 1000 cycles with no noticeable decay, indicating a long-term cycling stability in the cell. The appealing sodium ion storage characteristics combined with outstanding rate capability and cycling stability of both the NTO anode and PSC cathode in half cells is beneficial to improve the property when assembled into hybrid ion capacitors.</p><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/medium/nl-2016-02932h_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Electrochemical characteristics of urchin-like NTO and PSC in half cells. (a) The typical charge–discharge profiles of NTO between 0.01 and 2.5 V at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The corresponding rate capability (b) and cycling performance (c) with Coulombic efficiency over 1000 cycles at the current density of 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) The typical discharge–charge profiles of peanut shell carbon between 1.5 and 4.2 V at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The corresponding rate capability (e) and cycling performance (f) with Coulombic efficiency over 1000 cycles at the current density of 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>Following the detailed electrochemical characterization of the NTO anode and PSC cathode, a quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor using the sodium ion conducting gel polymer as the electrolyte is assembled and characterized. Shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a is a schematic illustration of the coin cell assembled and charge storage mechanism of the NIC with two ends concurrently constructed with high-performance NTO and PSC to overcome the kinetics discrepancy. During the charging process, the NTO anode undergoes reversible sodium ion insertion whereas the PSC cathode involves electric double layer capacitance with ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>–</sup> anions. The above reactions are reversed during the discharging process. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b displays the photos of the prepared porous P(VDF-HFP) membrane (top) and its gel polymer electrolyte (bottom). The color of the membrane changed from white to transparent, indicating the organic electrolyte successfully entrapped into the pores of the P(VDF-HFP) matrix. In <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c, the galvanostatic charge–discharge curves of the quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor at current densities from 0.4 to 3.2 A g<sup>–1</sup> displays a symmetric quasi-triangular shape, indicating the combination of the different storage mechanisms (faradaic reactions and nonfaradaic reactions). The Ragone plot in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d represents the trade-off between energy and power densities in the quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor described herein. A high-energy density of 111.2 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> is achieved at a power density of 800 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, which is calculated from the total mass of both electrodes. It can still retain an energy density of 33.2 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at a high-power density of 11200 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, demonstrating the exceptional power delivery of the present sodium ion system. It is instructive to compare the present urchin-like NTO//PSC device to the state-of-the-art reported sodium ion capacitors and other energy storage systems such as lithium ion capacitors and lithium ion batteries to clarify the high-energy–high-power feature of the proposed design. Although reasonable performances are obtained by reported literatures such as AC//MCMB, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> AC//V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>/CNT, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a> AC//Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>H<sub>2–<i>x</i></sub>Ti<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> PHPNC//TiC <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> and LMO//CN-LTO-NMS, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a> the sodium ion capacitor presented here demonstrates the most promising energy-power delivery. Moreover, our quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor using the sodium ion conducting gel polymer as the electrolyte even compare favorably with the device using liquid organic electrolyte (glass fiber as the separator). Indeed, unlike the present results, high-energy output is generally accompanied by a low power delivery (Figure S7, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). This is probably attributed to the higher sodium ionic conductivity of the gel polymer electrolyte than that of the commercial separator. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> Shown in Figure S8 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>) is the impedance plots of the urchin-like NTO//PSC NIC using the liquid electrolyte and quasi-solid-state electrolyte, respectively. The resistance of device using the gel polymer electrolyte is much less than that of the device using liquid electrolyte combined commercial glass fiber separator. This may be because the polarity of the P(VDF-HFP) matrix buffers the movement of large ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>–</sup> anions. The cycling stability of the urchin-like NTO//PSC quasi-solid-state NIC (shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>e) is investigated at the current density of 3.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>, and the device maintains its columbic efficiency approximately 100% up to 3000 cycles with capacity retention of approximately 86%. In contrast to half cells that demonstrate good cycling performance with no noticeable decay during cycle tests, the device showed capacitance decay. The possible reasons may be due to an increase in the interfacial resistance and loss of active sodium ions with cycling. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 39 and 40">(39, 40)</a></p><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/medium/nl-2016-02932h_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Electrochemical performance of the assembled quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitors. (a) Schematic of a coin cell type sodium ion capacitor. (b) Photos of the prepared porous P(VDF-HFP) membrane and its gel polymer electrolyte. (c) Galvanostatic charge–discharge curves from 0.5 to 3.5 V at different current densities. (d) Ragone plots for the urchin-like NTO//PSC compared with other literature works. The energy and power densities and capacitance were calculated based on the total weight of the anode and cathode materials. (e) Cycling stability of the quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitors.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>In order to explore the potential application of the present quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor, a flexible device is fabricated, following the significant trend of portable and wearable electronics that require high flexibility, performance, and safety. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41 ref42 ref43 ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref42 ref43 ref44" aria-label="reference 41 to 44">(41-44)</a> Figure S9 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>) schematically illustrates the fabrication process of the flexible quasi-solid-state NIC. The whole device, consisting of foil/poly bag film, gel polymer electrolyte, cathode and anode, is safer and thinner than the common liquid electrolyte-based hybrid device. No organic liquid electrolyte is used in the device or device fabrication, thus the designed NIC potentially increases the safety and reduce the complicated fabrication cost. Furthermore, the flexible quasi-solid-state NIC are efficient, compact, and they can fit the various size requirement of commercial electronics. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a shows the schematic illustration of the structure of a flexible quasi-solid-state NIC, which is sealed by two thin pieces of foil/poly bag film. To demonstrate the flexibility of the as-fabricated hybrid ion devices, the device is unrolled in flat and rolled with a mandrel of four different diameters (shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b,c inset) to evaluate its electrochemical behavior under different bending states. Encouragingly, there is no obvious capacity loss under different bending conditions, suggesting its remarkable mechanical robustness and great potential to be used for practical application. Furthermore, <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>d shows that the present flexible quasi-solid-state NIC is able to power a commercial desk lamp and a UT capacitor logo consisting of 50 red LEDs, demonstrating its high-energy–high-power characteristics.</p><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/medium/nl-2016-02932h_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) Schematic illustration of the structure of the quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor. (b) Diagram of the flexible quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor under various bending conditions. (c) Stability of capacitive performance of the quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor collected at different bending conditions (the inset shows the flexibility with different mandrel radius). (d) A commercial desk lamp and a UT capacitor logo consisting of 50 red LEDs powered by the assembled quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor under rolled state.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/asset/images/large/nl-2016-02932h_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="last">In summary, a quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor has been developed based on the urchin-like NTO and PSC as anode and cathode materials, respectively, using a sodium ion conducting gel polymer as electrolyte. Such a sodium ion capacitor can exhibit battery-like high-energy characteristics and a supercapacitor-like high power and long cycle life because of the integrated storage mechanisms. A maximum energy density of 111.2 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> can be achieved at a power density of 800 W kg<sup>–1</sup> based on the total mass of the electrode materials. The device can also exhibit an outstanding cycling stability with approximately 86% capacity retention after 3000 cycles. The observed superior electrochemical performance is among the best reported hybrid ion capacitors up to present. Furthermore, a flexible quasi-solid-state sodium ion capacitor is fabricated, and it is robust enough to work under harsh mechanical deformation conditions with no significant capacity loss. These findings provide an opportunity for the further development of hybrid ion capacitor for a wide range of high-energy–high-power required electronic applications.</p><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i1">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932" class="ext-link">10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Detailed experimental procedures and supplementary characterization methods including STEM, SEM, BET, CV, charge–discharge and EIS test of the prepared samples (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf">nl6b02932_si_001.pdf (1.65 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D materials. Graphene, related two-dimensional crystals, and hybrid systems for energy conversion and storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bonaccorso Francesco; Colombo Luigi; Yu Guihua; Stoller Meryl; Tozzini Valentina; Ferrari Andrea C; Ruoff Rodney S; Pellegrini Vittorio</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (New York, N.Y.)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">347</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6217</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1246501</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene and related two-dimensional crystals and hybrid systems showcase several key properties that can address emerging energy needs, in particular for the ever growing market of portable and wearable energy conversion and storage devices.  Graphene's flexibility, large surface area, and chemical stability, combined with its excellent electrical and thermal conductivity, make it promising as a catalyst in fuel and dye-sensitized solar cells.  Chemically functionalized graphene can also improve storage and diffusion of ionic species and electric charge in batteries and supercapacitors.  Two-dimensional crystals provide optoelectronic and photocatalytic properties complementing those of graphene, enabling the realization of ultrathin-film photovoltaic devices or systems for hydrogen production.  Here, we review the use of graphene and related materials for energy conversion and storage, outlining the roadmap for future applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcT59iv-p08Dl4vKgEt20y1XfW6udTcc2ea0YzI-orPCH7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2Mvjt1ektQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=f2b976cbe793eb220db317fa6a671714</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE02986K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Karpuzov, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kohandehghan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly confined ions store charge more efficiently in supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Merlet C; Pean C; Rotenberg B; Madden P A; Daffos B; Taberna P-L; Simon P; Salanne M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2701</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Liquids exhibit specific properties when they are adsorbed in nanoporous structures.  This is particularly true in the context of supercapacitors, for which an anomalous increase in performance has been observed for nanoporous electrodes.  This enhancement has been traditionally attributed in experimental studies to the effect of confinement of the ions from the electrolyte inside sub-nanometre pores, which is accompanied by their partial desolvation.  Here we perform molecular dynamics simulations of realistic supercapacitors and show that this picture is correct at the microscopic scale.  We provide a detailed analysis of the various environments experienced by the ions.  We pick out four different adsorption types, and we, respectively, label them as edge, planar, hollow and pocket sites upon increase of the coordination of the molecular species by carbon atoms from the electrode.  We show that both the desolvation and the local charge stored on the electrode increase with the degree of confinement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRwtPu7Tv7YzLGbPKh4T9eAfW6udTcc2ea0YzI-orPCH7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c7gsFyhug%253D%253D&amp;md5=5e2218af82446fa29e0e91d9cc111d16</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-014-0612-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bi, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">193</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">200</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s12274-014-0612-y</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DBi%252C%2BW.%253B%2BHu%252C%2BZ.%253B%2BLi%252C%2BX.%253B%2BWu%252C%2BC.%253B%2BWu%252C%2BJ.%253B%2BWu%252C%2BY.%253B%2BXie%252C%2BY.Nano%2BRes.%2B2015%252C%2B8%252C%2B193%25E2%2580%2593200&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs12274-014-0612-y&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metallic mesocrystal nanosheets of vanadium nitride for high-performance all-solid-state pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bi, Wentuan; Hu, Zhenpeng; Li, Xiaogang; Wu, Changzheng; Wu, Junchi; Wu, Yubin; Xie, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">193-200</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal nitrides (TMNs) are of particular interest by virtue of their synergic advantages of superior elec. cond., excellent environmental durability and high reaction selectivity, yet it is difficult to achieve flexible design and operation.  Herein, mesocrystal nanosheets (MCNSs) of vanadium nitride (VN) are synthesized via a confined-growth route from thermally stable layered vanadium bronze, representing the first two-dimensional (2D) metallic mesocrystal in inorg. compds.  Benefiting from their single-cryst.-like long-range electronic connectivity, VN MCNSs deliver an elec. cond. of 1.44 × 105 S/m at room temp., among the highest values obsd. for 2D nanosheets.  Coupled with their unique pseudocapacitance, VN MCNS-based flexible supercapacitors afford a superior volumetric capacitance of 1,937 mF/cm3.  Nitride MCNSs should have wide applications in the energy storage and conversion fields because their intrinsic high cond. is coupled with the reactivity of inorg. lattices. Rec.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2005</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">286</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">297</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/tcr.20054</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DScrosati%252C%2BB.Chem.%2BRec.%2B2005%252C%2B5%252C%2B286%25E2%2580%2593297&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Ftcr.20054&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Power sources for portable electronics and hybrid cars: Lithium batteries and fuel cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Scrosati, Bruno</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Record</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2005</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">286-297</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRHEAK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1527-8999</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The activities in progress in our lab. for the development of batteries and fuel cells for portable electronics and hybrid car applications are discussed.  In the case of lithium batteries, the research has been mainly focused on the characterization of new electrode and electrolyte materials.  Results related to disordered carbon anodes and improved, solvent-free, as well as gel-type, polymer electrolytes are particularly stressed.  It is shown that the use of proper gel electrolytes, in combination with suitable electrode couples, allows the development of new types of safe, reliable, and low-cost lithium-ion batteries which appear to be very promising power sources for hybrid vehicles.  Some of the technologies proven to be successful in the lithium battery area are readapted for use in fuel cells.  In particular, this approach has been followed for the prepn. of low-cost and stable protonic membranes to be proposed as an alternative to the expensive, perfluorosulfonic membranes presently used in polymer electrolyte membrane fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcYjIpK8OVMLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbUFN_7uMyyA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXht12ntb3J&amp;md5=ef9b0314e5777c69baa5228a2ded75b0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201402620"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">High-power Na-ion batteries have tremendous potential in various large-scale applications. The present work demonstrates that the pseudocapacitance of the nanosheet compd.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Excellent energy-power characteristics from a hybrid sodium ion capacitor based on identical carbon nanosheets in both electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Huanlei; Mitlin, David; Ding, Jia; Li, Zhi; Cui, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors created a hybrid Na ion capacitor (NIC) with a unique architecture and exceptional energy-power characteristics.  Both the anode and the cathode are based on peanut skin derived C nanosheets fabricated by simultaneous carbonization and activation or by carbonization alone.  The tens of nanometer thick (down to 20 nm) - high surface area (up to 2070 m2 g-1) nanosheets possesses a disordered structure for copious reversible binding of Na at the C defects.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensionally ordered porous TiNb2O7 nanotubes: a superior anode material for next generation hybrid supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hongsen; Shen, Laifa; Wang, Jie; Fang, Shan; Zhang, Yingxia; Dou, Hui; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid supercapacitors are a very appealing power source with high energy d. and power d. because they employ both the merits of lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors.  To balance such hybrid systems, the rate of the redox component must be substantially comparative to the levels of the double layer process.  As far as the insertion-host material TiNb2O7 is concerned, we have used facile step electrode design consisting of the phys. assisted template infusion of Ti-Nb sol into the pores of AAO followed by in situ conversion into porous TiNb2O7 nanotubes within the AAO walls under calcination, and finally making those templates dissolve away.  Using such an electrode as the battery type anode and a graphene grass electrode as the capacitor type cathode, we successfully constructed a novel hybrid supercapacitor.  Within a voltage range of 0-3 V, a high energy d. of ∼74 W h kg-1 is achieved and it could remain as much as ∼34.5 W h kg-1 at a power of 7500 W kg-1.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mechanical bending properties of sodium titanate (Na2Ti3O7) nanowires</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bo, Arixin; Zhan, Haifei; Bell, John; Zhu, Huaiyong; Gu, Yuantong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">100</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">56970-56976</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
