            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report on the mech. properties of sodium titanate nanowires (Na2Ti3O7 NW) through a combination of bending expts. and theor. anal.  Na2Ti3O7 NWs with lateral dimensions ranging from 20-700 nm were synthesized by a hydrothermal approach.  A focused ion beam (FIB) was used to manipulate the selected Na2Ti3O7 NW over a hole drilled in an indium tin oxide substrate.  After welding the nanowire, a series of bending tests was performed.  It was obsd. that the Na2Ti3O7 NW exhibits a brittle behavior, and a nonlinear elastic deformation was obsd. before failure.  By using the modified Euler-Bernoulli beam theory, such nonlinear elastic deformation is found to originate from a combination of surface effects and axial elongation (arising from the bending deformation).  The effective Young's modulus of the Na2Ti3O7 NW was found to be independent of the wire length, and ranges from 21.4 GPa to 45.5 GPa, with an av. value of 33 ± 7 GPa.  The yield strength of the Na2Ti3O7 NW is measured at 2.7 ± 0.7 GPa.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6PGSo0K3WprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIwaxADOpgZA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSltrvM&amp;md5=17fb1e6cb86caf384d89d3c05e1abfab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1107/S0365110X61003636"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Andersson, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wadsley, A.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Acta Crystallogr.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1961</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1245</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1249</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Taking steps forward in understanding the electrochemical behavior of Na2Ti3O7</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nava-Avendano, J.; Morales-Garcia, A.; Ponrouch, A.; Rousse, G.; Frontera, C.; Senguttuvan, P.; Tarascon, J.-M.; Dompablo, M. E. Arroyo-de; Palacin, M. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22280-22286</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na2Ti3O7 is an interesting neg. electrode material for sodium ion batteries given its electrochem. capacity and low operation potential.  Unfortunately its prospects of practical application are hindered by an unacceptable capacity fading upon cycling.  In this work we combine expts. and DFT calcns. to investigate the origin of such a phenomenon.  Different electrode technologies and different electrolytes have been targeted for electrochem. testing while the stability of Na2Ti3O7 and the fully reduced Na4Ti3O7 has been studied.  The calcd. elastic consts. and vibrational modes support the mech. and dynamical stability of the Na4Ti3O7 structure.  In situ XRD measurements corroborate the reversibility of the insertion reaction as no structural damage is detected after 50 cycles.  An intriguing reactivity of Na2Ti3O7 with the electrolyte upon storage is obsd., which coupled to electrochem. measurements points to this being the main factor behind capacity fading.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPiJfmTaTO_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgORfvoTWBwzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFaqtr7I&amp;md5=99423d2dca5159c6fd9ad4e648cf3cd1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/cm202076g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Senguttuvan, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rousse, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Seznec, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, J.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palacin, M. Commun.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2431</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms3431</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DWu%252C%2BC.%253B%2BLu%252C%2BX.%253B%2BPeng%252C%2BL.%253B%2BXu%252C%2BK.%253B%2BPeng%252C%2BX.%253B%2BHuang%252C%2BJ.%253B%2BYu%252C%2BG.%253B%2BXie%252C%2BY.Nat.%2BCommun.%2B2013%252C%2B4%252C%2B2431&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b02932&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms3431&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-dimensional vanadyl phosphate ultrathin nanosheets for high energy density and flexible pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu Changzheng; Lu Xiuli; Peng Lele; Xu Kun; Peng Xu; Huang Jianliu; Yu Guihua; Xie Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2431</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional materials have been an ideal material platform for constructing flexible ultrathin-film supercapacitors, offering great advantages of flexibility, ultra-thinness and even transparency.  Exploring new two-dimensional pseudocapacitive materials with high electrochemical activity is needed to achieve flexible ultrathin-film supercapacitors with higher energy densities.  Here we report an inorganic graphene analogue, α1-vanadyl phosphate ultrathin nanosheets with less than six atomic layers, as a promising material to construct a flexible ultrathin-film pseudocapacitor in all-solid-state.  The material exhibits a high potential plateau of ~ 1.0 V in aqueous solutions, approaching the electrochemical potential window of water (1.23 V).  The as-established flexible supercapacitor achieves a high redox potential (1.0 V) and a high areal capacitance of 8,360.5 μF cm(-2), leading to a high energy density of 1.7 mWh cm(-2) and a power density of 5.2 mW cm(-2).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQtavUaLESyEIHWj6b1v8uTfW6udTcc2eb_XIvNwS1GNbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sbntl2rtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=46dbbde11ea3f0aec93dd1493a291ca2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201301941"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D materials. Graphene, related two-dimensional crystals, and hybrid systems for energy conversion and storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bonaccorso Francesco; Colombo Luigi; Yu Guihua; Stoller Meryl; Tozzini Valentina; Ferrari Andrea C; Ruoff Rodney S; Pellegrini Vittorio</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (New York, N.Y.)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">347</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6217</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1246501</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene and related two-dimensional crystals and hybrid systems showcase several key properties that can address emerging energy needs, in particular for the ever growing market of portable and wearable energy conversion and storage devices.  Graphene's flexibility, large surface area, and chemical stability, combined with its excellent electrical and thermal conductivity, make it promising as a catalyst in fuel and dye-sensitized solar cells.  Chemically functionalized graphene can also improve storage and diffusion of ionic species and electric charge in batteries and supercapacitors.  Two-dimensional crystals provide optoelectronic and photocatalytic properties complementing those of graphene, enabling the realization of ultrathin-film photovoltaic devices or systems for hydrogen production.  Here, we review the use of graphene and related materials for energy conversion and storage, outlining the roadmap for future applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcT59iv-p08Dl4vKgEt20y1XfW6udTcc2eZSqhmtF3CWHrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2Mvjt1ektQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=f2b976cbe793eb220db317fa6a671714</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE02986K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Karpuzov, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kohandehghan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                 10.1038/ncomms3701</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly confined ions store charge more efficiently in supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Merlet C; Pean C; Rotenberg B; Madden P A; Daffos B; Taberna P-L; Simon P; Salanne M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2701</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Liquids exhibit specific properties when they are adsorbed in nanoporous structures.  This is particularly true in the context of supercapacitors, for which an anomalous increase in performance has been observed for nanoporous electrodes.  This enhancement has been traditionally attributed in experimental studies to the effect of confinement of the ions from the electrolyte inside sub-nanometre pores, which is accompanied by their partial desolvation.  Here we perform molecular dynamics simulations of realistic supercapacitors and show that this picture is correct at the microscopic scale.  We provide a detailed analysis of the various environments experienced by the ions.  We pick out four different adsorption types, and we, respectively, label them as edge, planar, hollow and pocket sites upon increase of the coordination of the molecular species by carbon atoms from the electrode.  We show that both the desolvation and the local charge stored on the electrode increase with the degree of confinement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRwtPu7Tv7YzLGbPKh4T9eAfW6udTcc2eZSqhmtF3CWHrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c7gsFyhug%253D%253D&amp;md5=5e2218af82446fa29e0e91d9cc111d16</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-014-0612-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bi, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">193</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">200</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">193-200</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal nitrides (TMNs) are of particular interest by virtue of their synergic advantages of superior elec. cond., excellent environmental durability and high reaction selectivity, yet it is difficult to achieve flexible design and operation.  Herein, mesocrystal nanosheets (MCNSs) of vanadium nitride (VN) are synthesized via a confined-growth route from thermally stable layered vanadium bronze, representing the first two-dimensional (2D) metallic mesocrystal in inorg. compds.  Benefiting from their single-cryst.-like long-range electronic connectivity, VN MCNSs deliver an elec. cond. of 1.44 × 105 S/m at room temp., among the highest values obsd. for 2D nanosheets.  Coupled with their unique pseudocapacitance, VN MCNS-based flexible supercapacitors afford a superior volumetric capacitance of 1,937 mF/cm3.  Nitride MCNSs should have wide applications in the energy storage and conversion fields because their intrinsic high cond. is coupled with the reactivity of inorg. lattices.                         rightTab-cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Power sources for portable electronics and hybrid cars: Lithium batteries and fuel cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Scrosati, Bruno</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Record</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2005</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">286-297</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The activities in progress in our lab. for the development of batteries and fuel cells for portable electronics and hybrid car applications are discussed.  In the case of lithium batteries, the research has been mainly focused on the characterization of new electrode and electrolyte materials.  Results related to disordered carbon anodes and improved, solvent-free, as well as gel-type, polymer electrolytes are particularly stressed.  It is shown that the use of proper gel electrolytes, in combination with suitable electrode couples, allows the development of new types of safe, reliable, and low-cost lithium-ion batteries which appear to be very promising power sources for hybrid vehicles.  Some of the technologies proven to be successful in the lithium battery area are readapted for use in fuel cells.  In particular, this approach has been followed for the prepn. of low-cost and stable protonic membranes to be proposed as an alternative to the expensive, perfluorosulfonic membranes presently used in polymer electrolyte membrane fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcYjIpK8OVMLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljiMI8OG55Udg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXht12ntb3J&amp;md5=ef9b0314e5777c69baa5228a2ded75b0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201402620"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitance of MXene nanosheets for high-power sodium-ion hybrid capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xianfen; Kajiyama, Satoshi; Iinuma, Hiroki; Hosono, Eiji; Oro, Shinji; Moriguchi, Isamu; Okubo, Masashi; Yamada, Atsuo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6544</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-power Na-ion batteries have tremendous potential in various large-scale applications.  However, conventional charge storage through ion intercalation or double-layer formation cannot satisfy the requirements of such applications owing to the slow kinetics of ion intercalation and the small capacitance of the double layer.  The present work demonstrates that the pseudocapacitance of the nanosheet compd. MXene Ti2C achieves a higher specific capacity relative to double-layer capacitor electrodes and a higher rate capability relative to ion intercalation electrodes.  By utilizing the pseudocapacitance as a neg. electrode, the prototype Na-ion full cell consisting of an alluaudite Na2Fe2(SO4)3 pos. electrode and an MXene Ti2C neg. electrode operates at a relatively high voltage of 2.4 V and delivers 90 and 40 mAh g-1 at 1.0 and 5.0 A g-1 (based on the wt. of the neg. electrode), resp., which are not attainable by conventional electrochem. energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGbG1IuL6ZLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYV5bNla2JhQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXotlaitrg%253D&amp;md5=b97a6937c162bb790a4949b87257c217</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA01392A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, K.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem.                         rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Excellent energy-power characteristics from a hybrid sodium ion capacitor based on identical carbon nanosheets in both electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Huanlei; Mitlin, David; Ding, Jia; Li, Zhi; Cui, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5149-5158</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors created a hybrid Na ion capacitor (NIC) with a unique architecture and exceptional energy-power characteristics.  Both the anode and the cathode are based on peanut skin derived C nanosheets fabricated by simultaneous carbonization and activation or by carbonization alone.  The tens of nanometer thick (down to 20 nm) - high surface area (up to 2070 m2 g-1) nanosheets possesses a disordered structure for copious reversible binding of Na at the C defects.  They are also hierarchically micro-meso-macro porous, allowing facile ion transport at high rates both through the pore-filling electrolyte and in the solid-state.  When employed as Na ion battery anode, the C shows a tremendous reversible (desodiation) capacity of 461 mA-h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and excellent rate capability, e.g. 107 mA-h g-1 at 5 A g-1.  The optimized NIC device displays highly favorable Ragone chart placement, e.g. 112 and 45 W h kg-1 at 67 and 12,000 W kg-1, retaining 85% of its capacity after 3000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQtRgPkbkw0bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYV5bNla2JhQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XktVags7c%253D&amp;md5=0d8dd4ea44f030f854242460d05d92ea</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA02929E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                 10.1039/C5TA02929E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensionally ordered porous TiNb2O7 nanotubes: a superior anode material for next generation hybrid supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hongsen; Shen, Laifa; Wang, Jie; Fang, Shan; Zhang, Yingxia; Dou, Hui; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">32</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16785-16790</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid supercapacitors are a very appealing power source with high energy d. and power d. because they employ both the merits of lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors.  To balance such hybrid systems, the rate of the redox component must be substantially comparative to the levels of the double layer process.  As far as the insertion-host material TiNb2O7 is concerned, we have used facile step electrode design consisting of the phys. assisted template infusion of Ti-Nb sol into the pores of AAO followed by in situ conversion into porous TiNb2O7 nanotubes within the AAO walls under calcination, and finally making those templates dissolve away.  Using such an electrode as the battery type anode and a graphene grass electrode as the capacitor type cathode, we successfully constructed a novel hybrid supercapacitor.  Within a voltage range of 0-3 V, a high energy d. of ∼74 W h kg-1 is achieved and it could remain as much as ∼34.5 W h kg-1 at a power of 7500 W kg-1.  The present research sheds new light on the development of energy storage devices with both high energy d. and high power d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVAhusU4IMu7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYV5bNla2JhQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFGns7nJ&amp;md5=c9d02d6b7b90e35f6524d2143f3fccbb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1021/nn501972w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lim, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ku, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mechanical bending properties of sodium titanate (Na2Ti3O7) nanowires</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bo, Arixin; Zhan, Haifei; Bell, John; Zhu, Huaiyong; Gu, Yuantong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">100</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">56970-56976</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report on the mech. properties of sodium titanate nanowires (Na2Ti3O7 NW) through a combination of bending expts. and theor. anal.  Na2Ti3O7 NWs with lateral dimensions ranging from 20-700 nm were synthesized by a hydrothermal approach.  A focused ion beam (FIB) was used to manipulate the selected Na2Ti3O7 NW over a hole drilled in an indium tin oxide substrate.  After welding the nanowire, a series of bending tests was performed.  It was obsd. that the Na2Ti3O7 NW exhibits a brittle behavior, and a nonlinear elastic deformation was obsd. before failure.  By using the modified Euler-Bernoulli beam theory, such nonlinear elastic deformation is found to originate from a combination of surface effects and axial elongation (arising from the bending deformation).  The effective Young's modulus of the Na2Ti3O7 NW was found to be independent of the wire length, and ranges from 21.4 GPa to 45.5 GPa, with an av. value of 33 ± 7 GPa.  The yield strength of the Na2Ti3O7 NW is measured at 2.7 ± 0.7 GPa.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6PGSo0K3WprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYV5bNla2JhQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSltrvM&amp;md5=17fb1e6cb86caf384d89d3c05e1abfab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1107/S0365110X61003636"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Andersson, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wadsley, A.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Acta Crystallogr.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1961</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1245</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1249</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na2Ti3O7 is an interesting neg. electrode material for sodium ion batteries given its electrochem. capacity and low operation potential.  Unfortunately its prospects of practical application are hindered by an unacceptable capacity fading upon cycling.  In this work we combine expts. and DFT calcns. to investigate the origin of such a phenomenon.  Different electrode technologies and different electrolytes have been targeted for electrochem. testing while the stability of Na2Ti3O7 and the fully reduced Na4Ti3O7 has been studied.  The calcd. elastic consts. and vibrational modes support the mech. and dynamical stability of the Na4Ti3O7 structure.  In situ XRD measurements corroborate the reversibility of the insertion reaction as no structural damage is detected after 50 cycles.  An intriguing reactivity of Na2Ti3O7 with the electrolyte upon storage is obsd., which coupled to electrochem. measurements points to this being the main factor behind capacity fading.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPiJfmTaTO_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljTFSCVi4IS4Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFaqtr7I&amp;md5=99423d2dca5159c6fd9ad4e648cf3cd1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1021/cm202076g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Senguttuvan, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rousse, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Seznec, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, J.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palacin, M. Ed.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">55</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">7474</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">7477</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms3431"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peng, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peng, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Commun.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2431</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms3431</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-dimensional vanadyl phosphate ultrathin nanosheets for high energy density and flexible pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu Changzheng; Lu Xiuli; Peng Lele; Xu Kun; Peng Xu; Huang Jianliu; Yu Guihua; Xie Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2431</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional materials have been an ideal material platform for constructing flexible ultrathin-film supercapacitors, offering great advantages of flexibility, ultra-thinness and even transparency.  Exploring new two-dimensional pseudocapacitive materials with high electrochemical activity is needed to achieve flexible ultrathin-film supercapacitors with higher energy densities.  Here we report an inorganic graphene analogue, α1-vanadyl phosphate ultrathin nanosheets with less than six atomic layers, as a promising material to construct a flexible ultrathin-film pseudocapacitor in all-solid-state.  The material exhibits a high potential plateau of ~ 1.0 V in aqueous solutions, approaching the electrochemical potential window of water (1.23 V).  The as-established flexible supercapacitor achieves a high redox potential (1.0 V) and a high areal capacitance of 8,360.5 μF cm(-2), leading to a high energy density of 1.7 mWh cm(-2) and a power density of 5.2 mW cm(-2).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQtavUaLESyEIHWj6b1v8uTfW6udTcc2earCGYEorT8Ebntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sbntl2rtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=46dbbde11ea3f0aec93dd1493a291ca2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201301941"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, S. Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ko, S. H.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">52</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">7718</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">7723</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.201301941</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i1">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932" class="ext-link">10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Detailed experimental procedures and supplementary characterization methods including STEM, SEM, BET, CV, charge–discharge and EIS test of the prepared samples (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02932/suppl_file/nl6b02932_si_001.pdf">nl6b02932_si_001.pdf (1.65 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6e28f9f97775c-LHR">
var currentJournal = "Nano Letters";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
